The Uncreated Quran and Its Manifestation
Affirmation of the uncreated Quran and its manifestation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Salaf doctrine that the Quran is uncreated and how it is recited, written, and heard without separation from Allah.

Core Idea
The Quran is one eternal speech manifesting in temporal forms without division.

This passage presents the orthodox Sunni position on the nature of the Quran. The author rejects later innovations that divide speech into internal and verbal, affirming instead the Salaf's understanding that God's speech is one and undivided. Even though we recite, write, and hear the Quran, it remains the eternal speech of Allah, not a created thing. This lesson will unpack that claim and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's strong language against dividing divine speech.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three manifestations
Find the phrases describing how the Quran manifests on hearts, tongues, in books, and in ears. Note the Arabic terms: مفهوم، منطوق، منقوش، مسموع.
These four forms are all the same eternal speech.
3
Understand the analogy
The author uses a Persian couplet about clothes changing but not harming the person. Reflect on how multiplicity of manifestation does not affect the thing manifested.
This counters the objection that the recited Quran must be created.
4
Grasp the limitation of reason
The passage ends with a call to believe without grasping the essence. Appreciate the role of faith and authority in accepting this doctrine.
This is a common theme in kalam: iman bi al-jumla.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحق عندنا أن التنويع إلى النفسي واللفظي إنما مال إليه المتأخرون إفحاما للمعتزلة وإفهاما للعقول السافلة، كما اختاروا في المتشابهات مسلك التأويل، وإنما المذهب ما عليه أئمة السلف أن كلام الله تعالى واحد لا تعدد فيه أصلا، لم ينفصل ولن ينفصل عن الرحمن، ولا أوراق ولا آذان، ومع ذلك ليس المحفوظ في صدورنا إلا هو، ولا المتلو بأفواهنا إلا هو، ولا المكتوب في مصاحفنا إلا هو، ولا المسموع بأسماعنا إلا هو، لا يحل لأحد أن يقول بحدوث المحفوظ المتلو المكتوب المسموع، إنما الحادث نحن وحفظنا وألسننا وتلاوتنا وأيدينا وكتابتنا وآذاننا وسماعتنا والقرآن القديم القائم بذات الله تعالى، هو المتجلي على قلوبنا بكسوة المفهوم، وألسنتنا بصورة المنطوق، ومصاحفنا بلباس المنقوش، وآذاننا بزي المسموع فهو المفهوم المنطوق المنقوش المسموع لا شيء آخر غيره دالا عليه. وذلك من دون أن يكون له انفصال عن الله سبحانه وتعالى، أو اتصال بالحوادث أو حلول في شيء مما ذكر، وكيف يحل القديم في الحادث، ولا وجود للحادث مع القديم، إنما الوجود للقديم وللحادث منه إضافة لتكريم، ومعلوم أن تعدد التجلي لا يقتضي تعدد المتجلي. و قد قيل: لباس گشت بدل شخص صاحب لباس را چه خلل. عرف هذا من عرف، ومن لم يقدر على فهمه فعليه أن يؤمن به كما يؤمن بالله وسائر صفاته من دون إدراك الكنه المعتمد المستند، ص٣٥)
And the truth according to us is that the division into internal (nafsi) and verbal (lafzi) was only adopted by the later scholars to refute the Mu'tazila and to make understand the inferior intellects, just as they chose the path of ta'wil (interpretation) for the ambiguous verses. Rather, the correct school is that of the imams of the Salaf: that the speech of Allah Most High is one, having no multiplicity at all; it did not separate and will not separate from the Most Merciful, nor [enter] papers nor ears. Nevertheless, what is preserved in our breasts is only It, what is recited by our mouths is only It, what is written in our mushafs (copies of the Qur'an) is only It, what is heard by our ears is only It. It is not permissible for anyone to say that the preserved, recited, written, heard [Qur'an] is created. Rather, what is created is we and our memory, our tongues, our recitation, our hands, our writing, our ears, and our hearing. The Qur'an is eternal, subsisting by the essence of Allah Most High. It manifests itself upon our hearts in the garment of understanding, upon our tongues in the form of uttered speech, in our mushafs in the dress of inscription, and in our ears in the guise of hearing. So it is the understood, uttered, inscribed, heard [thing]; there is nothing else other than it signifying it. That is without any separation from Allah Glorified and Exalted, nor connection with temporal things, nor indwelling in any of what was mentioned. How could the eternal indwell in the temporal, and there is no existence of the temporal with the eternal? Existence is only for the eternal, and for the temporal from Him is an added honoring. It is known that multiplicity of manifestation does not necessitate multiplicity of the manifested. And it has been said: 'Clothes change, but what harm to the person wearing the clothes?' He who knows this, knows; and he who cannot understand it must believe in it as he believes in Allah and His other attributes, without grasping the essence, relying on the authority, p. 35.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement affirming the Salafi position on the nature of divine speech (kalam Allah). The author begins by rejecting the division of speech into internal (nafsi) and verbal (lafzi) as a later innovation used to refute the Mu'tazila and accommodate inferior minds. He asserts that the true doctrine of the Salaf imams is that God's speech is one and undivided, never separating from God. Despite this, the Quran that is memorized, recited, written, and heard is the very same eternal speech, not a created thing. The created aspects are only the human acts of preserving, reciting, writing, and hearing. The Quran, being eternal, manifests itself in these forms without any partition, connection, or indwelling in temporal things. The author uses the analogy of a person wearing different clothes: changing clothes does not harm the person. He concludes that one must believe this without attempting to grasp its essence, relying on authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The recited Quran is a separate created thing that points to the eternal speech.
Correction: According to the Salaf, the recited Quran is the very eternal speech itself manifesting without separation or creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the eternal Quran and its recited, written, and heard forms?
A) The recited Quran is a separate created thing that indicates the eternal speech.
B) The recited Quran is the eternal speech itself manifesting without separation.
C) The eternal speech is only the meaning, while the words are created.
D) The recited Quran is a temporal copy of an eternal original in heaven.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is one eternal speech that manifests in multiple forms without division or creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe that you are encountering the very uncreated speech of Allah, not just a representation or a created copy? How does this conviction affect the reverence and attention you give to each verse?
?
The passage says the Quran manifests in your heart in the 'garment of understanding.' Are you satisfied with the depth of your understanding? What concrete steps will you take this week to remove barriers that prevent the Quran from being deeply understood in your heart?
?
The author warns against anyone saying the preserved, recited, written, or heard Quran is created. Have you ever, even inadvertently, thought of the mushaf as a mere book or the recitation as a human production? How can you train your heart to always perceive the eternal speech behind the temporal forms?

The Eternal Speech of Allah and Its Manifestation
The author explains the correct belief about the Qur'an as eternal speech and its manifestation in created forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that the Qur'an is the eternal speech of Allah, which manifests in created forms without becoming created.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is one eternal speech, manifesting in our recitation without being created.

This lesson delves into a critical point of Sunni creed: the nature of the Qur'an. The author clarifies that the Qur'an we recite, write, and hear is not a created entity but the very eternal speech of Allah, manifesting in our physical forms without separation or indwelling. This teaching guards against the Mu'tazila claim that the Qur'an is created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the author's firm stance and the key terms like qadīm (eternal) and ḥādith (originated).
2
Identify the rejection of the nafsī/lafẓī division
The author begins by rejecting the later distinction between internal and verbal speech. Understand why this distinction was introduced and why the Salaf position is upheld.
3
Understand the Salaf position
The Salaf hold that Allah's speech is one, indivisible, and not separate from Him. The Qur'an we memorize, recite, write, and hear is that same eternal speech.
4
Grasp the concept of manifestation (tajallī)
The eternal speech manifests in our hearts, tongues, scripts, and ears without being created. What is created are our actions, not the speech itself.
5
Reflect on the analogy and conclusion
The analogy of garments shows that changing manifestations do not affect the essence. Conclude by accepting this belief, even if one cannot fully comprehend it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحق عندنا أن التنويع إلى النفسي واللفظي إنما مال إليه المتأخرون إفحاما للمعتزلة وإفهام للعقول السافلة، كما اختاروا في المتشابهات مسلك التاويل، وإنما المذهب ما عليه أئمة السلف أنّ کلام تعالى واحد لا تعدد فيه أصلا، لم ينفصل ولن ينفصل عن الرحمن، ولا أوراق ولا آذان، ومع ذلك ليس المحفوظ في صدورنا إلا هو، ولا المتلو بأفواهنا إلا هو، ولا المكتوب في مصاحفنا إلا هو، ولا المسموع بأسماعنا إلا هو، لا يحل لأحد أن يقول بحدوث المحفوظ المتلو المكتوب المسموع، إنما الحادث نحن وحفظنا وألسننا وتلاوتنا وأيدينا وكتابتنا وآذاننا وسماعتنا والقرآن القديم القائم بذته تعالى، هو المتجلي على قلوبنا بكسوة المفهوم، وألسنتنا بصورة المنطوق، ومصاحفنا بلباس المنقوش، وآذاننا بزي المسموع فهو المفهوم المنطوق المنقوش المسموع لا شيء آخر غيره دالا عليه. وذلك من دون أن يكون له انفصال عن الله سبحانه وتعالى، أو اتصال بالحوادث أو حلول في شيء مما ذكر ، وكيف يحل القديم في الحادث، ولا وجود للحادث مع القديم، إنما الوجود للقديم وللحادث منه إضافة لتكريم، ومعلوم أن تعدد التجلي لا يقتضي تعدد المتجلي. و میدم گر لباس گشت بدل شخص صاحب لباس را چه خلل عرف هذا من عرف، ومن لم يقدر على فهمه فعليه أن يؤمن به كما يؤمن بالله وسائر صفاته من دون إدراك الكنه المعتمد المستند، ص٣٥)
The truth according to us is that the division into internal (nafsī) and verbal (lafẓī) speech was only adopted by later scholars to silence the Mu'tazila and teach inferior intellects, just as they chose the path of ta'wīl (allegorical interpretation) for ambiguous verses. Rather, the correct school is what the Salaf imams are upon: that the speech of the Exalted is one, with no multiplicity at all, it has not separated and will not separate from the Most Merciful, and neither papers nor ears [affect it]. Nevertheless, what is preserved in our hearts is only it, what is recited by our mouths is only it, what is written in our copies of the Qur'an is only it, and what is heard by our ears is only it. It is not permissible for anyone to say that the preserved, recited, written, and heard [Qur'an] is created (ḥādith). Rather, what is created is we, our memorization, our tongues, our recitation, our hands, our writing, our ears, and our hearing. The Qur'an is eternal (qadīm), subsisting in His essence, Exalted is He. It manifests upon our hearts in the garment of meaning, upon our tongues in the form of utterance, in our copies of the Qur'an in the dress of inscription, and upon our ears in the attire of sound. So it is the understood, uttered, inscribed, and heard – nothing else besides it indicates it. This is without it having separation from Allah, or connection with accidents, or indwelling in any of what was mentioned. How could the eternal indwell in the originated? And there is no existence of the originated along with the eternal. Existence belongs only to the eternal, and the originated has from it an addition for honor. It is known that the multiplicity of manifestations does not necessitate multiplicity of the manifested. And if a garment changes, what harm to the person wearing the garment? Whoever knows this knows it; and whoever is unable to comprehend it must believe in it just as he believes in Allah and His other attributes, without grasping the reality, relying on the authority [of those who know], (p. 35).
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage defines the correct Sunni doctrine regarding the nature of the Qur'an as the eternal speech of Allah. The author begins by rejecting the later division of speech into internal and verbal, attributing this innovation to attempts to refute the Mu'tazila and simplify matters for weak minds. The true position of the Salaf is that Allah's speech is one, eternal, indivisible, and not separate from Him. Nevertheless, the Qur'an that we memorize, recite, write, and hear is precisely that eternal speech, not something else. It is forbidden to say that the preserved, recited, written, or heard Qur'an is created. What is created are our actions and organs. The eternal Qur'an manifests itself in these forms without being separated from Allah or becoming incarnate in creatures. The author uses the analogy of a person wearing different garments to illustrate that changing manifestations do not affect the essence. He concludes by advising those who cannot grasp this to simply believe it without seeking full comprehension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'an that we recite and write is a created entity or a copy of an eternal original.
Correction: The Qur'an we interact with is the very eternal speech of Allah itself, not created. What is created are our actions (recitation, writing) but not the speech itself.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view regarding the Qur'an that is recited, written, and heard?
A) It is a created thing that points to Allah's speech
B) It is the eternal speech of Allah itself, not something else
C) It is a temporal copy of an eternal original
D) It is both created and eternal

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an we recite, write, and hear is the eternal speech of Allah, manifested in created forms without being created itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly believe that the words on your tongue are identical to the eternal speech of Allah, uncreated and subsisting in His essence? How does this belief affect the reverence and presence of heart you bring to each verse?
?
If your recitation is merely a created act, but the speech itself is eternal and unchanging, are you reciting as if you are in direct contact with the divine, or do you let your mind wander as if it is just words? What must change in your practice?
?
The author says that multiplicity of manifestations does not necessitate multiplicity of the manifested. Realizing that the Qur'an heard in different recitations is still one eternal speech, how does this unify your experience with the global Muslim community? Are you listening for the eternal reality behind the sound?

The Eternal Quran Present in Four Modes
Defense of the Quran's eternal presence in four modes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the orthodox Sunni doctrine that the Quran, as an eternal attribute of Allah, is truly present in its four modes of existence (recitation, hearing, writing, memorization) without being created or separated from the divine essence.

Core Idea
The Quran is one eternal attribute manifest in all four modes, not a created copy.

This passage clarifies a central point of Islamic theology: how the eternal Quran relates to our physical acts of recitation, writing, and memorization. The author defends the salaf's position that the Quran itself—the uncreated attribute—is what we actually recite, hear, write, and preserve. This lesson unpacks that profound claim and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold.
Notice the emphatic tone: 'فالقرآن الذي هو صفة قديمة...'
2
Identify the four modes
The passage explicitly states that the Quran is present in four modes: recited by tongues, heard by ears, written in lines, memorized in hearts. Find the Arabic for each.
These are the four 'مواطن' (loci) mentioned.
3
Understand what the author negates
The passage denies several misconceptions: the Quran is not a separate indicator, not connected to contingent things, not indwelling, not affected by newness. Reflect on why these negations are necessary.
These negations safeguard divine transcendence.
4
Reflect on the doctrine of tajalli
The author says these modes are 'manifestations' (تجليات) of the Quran. Consider what this means for the relationship between the eternal attribute and physical phenomena.
Tajalli explains how the one eternal Quran can be present in many forms without division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكن عقيدة ألمتنا السلف الحقة الصادقة أن هذه الأنحاء الأربعة كلها مواطن وجود القرآن العظيم حقيقة وحقا، ومجالي شهود الفرقان الكريم تحقيقا وصدقا، فالقرآن الذي هو صفة قديمة لحضرة العزة جلاله وقائم أزلا وأبدا بذاته الكريمة مستحيل الانفكاك عنه، ولا هو ولا غيره، ولا خالق ولا مخلوق، هو بعينه المقرو بلساننا، المسموع بآذاننا المكتوب في سطورنا ، المحفوظ في صدورنا والحمد لله رب العالمين. لا أنه آخر غير القرآن دالا على القرآن كلا! بل كلها تجلياته وهو المتجلي فيها حقيقة من دون أن ينفصل عن الذات الإلهية أو يتصل بشيء من الحوادث أو يكون له حلول فيه أو يصيب ذيل قدمه شية من حدوث تلك الكسوات أو يتطرق إليه.
But the true and sincere creed of our salaf imams is that these four modes are all loci of the existence of the Mighty Quran truly and really, and manifestations of witnessing the Noble Criterion (al-Furqan) genuinely and truly. So the Quran, which is an eternal attribute of the presence of Might (majesty be His) and subsisting eternally and forever with His noble essence, impossible to be separated from Him—neither He nor other, neither Creator nor created—is precisely what is recited by our tongues, heard by our ears, written in our lines, preserved in our hearts, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. It is not another thing besides the Quran indicating the Quran, no! Rather, all of them are His manifestations, and He is the one manifested in them truly, without being separated from the divine essence or being connected to any contingent thing, or having indwelling in it, or the hem of His garment being touched by any newness of those coverings, or that it should be subject to change.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanatory statement defending the orthodox Sunni view of the Quran as an eternal divine attribute. The author declares that the four modes of existence (external, mental, verbal, written) are all true loci for the Quran's existence. The Quran itself is an eternal attribute subsisting with Allah's essence, neither Creator nor created. It is precisely the same Quran that we recite with our tongues, hear with our ears, write in our lines, and memorize in our hearts. It is not a separate entity pointing to the Quran; rather, these modes are manifestations (tajalliyat) of the Quran. The Quran manifests in them without separation from the divine essence, without being connected to contingent things, without indwelling, and without being affected by the newness of these coverings (i.e., the physical letters and sounds). This safeguards divine transcendence while affirming the reality of the Quran in human experience.

Key Terms

القرآن
تجليات
حلول
حوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the recited or written Quran is a created copy separate from the eternal attribute.
Correction: The passage asserts that the Quran itself—the eternal attribute—is what is recited, heard, written, and memorized. It is not a separate created thing but the same attribute manifest in these modes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the Quran relate to its recitation, writing, and memorization?
A) The recited Quran is a created copy indicating the eternal Quran.
B) The Quran is the same eternal attribute manifest in all these modes.
C) The Quran becomes created when recited.
D) The Quran is only eternal in the mind, not in speech or writing.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the eternal attribute of Allah, truly present in our recitation, hearing, writing, and memorization without being created or separated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe that the very words you utter are the eternal attribute of Allah? If so, how does that change your attention and reverence during recitation? If not, what is the disconnect?
?
The passage says the Quran is 'neither He nor other, neither Creator nor created.' Have you ever regarded the Quran as something separate from Allah, a created object? Reflect on how this lesson challenges that view and how you will adjust your belief.
?
You have memorized some of the Quran in your heart. According to this lesson, that memorization is a locus of the Quran's existence. Does this give you a sense of responsibility for what you carry? How will you honor that treasure?

Divine Attributes

Pre-eternity and Permanence as Negative Attributes
The author argues that qidam and baqa' are negative attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why pre-eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa') are classified as negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) in Sunni kalam, not positive additions to Allah's essence.

Core Idea
Pre-eternity and permanence simply deny non-existence from Allah.

In this lesson, the author clarifies a subtle but important point about the divine attributes qidam and baqa'. Although some scholars count them among the positive attributes, the author argues they are actually negative because they only negate non-existence. We will follow his reasoning and see how it ties into the broader kalam framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
Pay attention to the logical connectors: 'ثم لما ثبت' (then when it is established), 'لأن' (because), 'فيرجع' (so it reverts).
2
Understand the argument
Identify the steps: (1) All existents end with the Necessary Being. (2) Non-existence is impossible for Him. (3) Therefore He is qadim and baqi. (4) The meanings of qidam and baqa' revert to negation of non-existence. (5) Thus they are negative attributes.
Notice why some counted them as positive – because they sound like positive descriptions, but the author shows they are merely negations.
3
Reflect on the quote from al-Turbashti
Al-Turbashti said that 'al-Mawjud' and 'al-Qadim' are names of the Essence. Consider what this implies about the attributes: they do not add something over and above the essence.
This supports the author's point that qidam is not a positive attribute but a name of the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما ثبت انتهاء الموجودات إلى واجب الوجود لذاته، والعدم على الواجب ممتنع، لأن ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه لزم كونه أزليا أبديا، فهو قديم لا أول لوجوده، وباق لا آخر لشهوده، فيرجع معنى القدم والبقاء في حقه سبحانه وتعالى إلى الصفات السلبية وإن عدهما بعضهم في النعوت الثبوتية؛ لأن معنى البقاء في حقه سبحانه وتعالى نفي عدم لاحق في الأبد، كما أن القدم عبارة عن نفي عدم سابق في الأزل فيرجع معناهما إلى نفي العدم، ولذا قال التوربشتي في معتقده: إن الموجود والقديم من أسماء الذات.
Then, when it is established that existents end with the Necessary Being in itself (Wajib al-Wujud li-dhatihi), and non-existence is impossible for the Necessary, because what is proven to have pre-eternity (qidam) cannot cease to exist, it follows that He is eternal and everlasting. Thus He is pre-eternal (qadim) with no beginning to His existence, and permanent (baqi) with no end to His witnessing. So the meaning of pre-eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa') with respect to Him, glorified and exalted, reverts to negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbiyya), even though some count them among the positive attributes (al-nu'ut al-thubutiyya). This is because the meaning of permanence with respect to Him is the negation of subsequent non-existence in eternity, just as pre-eternity is an expression of the negation of prior non-existence in pre-eternity. So their meaning reverts to the negation of non-existence. Therefore al-Turbashti said in his creed: 'Indeed, the Existent (al-mawjud) and the Pre-eternal (al-qadim) are among the names of the Essence.'
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of the attributes of pre-eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa') as applied to Allah. The argument proceeds as follows: It has been established that all contingent existents terminate at the Necessary Being in itself (Wajib al-Wujud li-dhatihi). Non-existence ('adam) is impossible for the Necessary, because whatever has been proven to have pre-eternity cannot cease to exist. Consequently, He must be eternal (azali) and everlasting (abadi). He is pre-eternal (qadim) with no beginning to His existence, and permanent (baqi) with no end to His being witnessed. From this, the author concludes that the meanings of pre-eternity and permanence in Allah's case revert to negative attributes (sifat salbiyya), meaning they are essentially negations of non-existence. Even though some scholars count them among the positive attributes (sifat thubutiyya), the author clarifies that they are actually negative because they deny non-existence: baqa' denies subsequent non-existence in the future, and qidam denies prior non-existence in the past. Thus both reduce to the negation of non-existence. The author supports this by quoting al-Turbashti, who stated that 'the Existent' and 'the Pre-eternal' are names of the Essence (dhat), implying they do not add a positive attribute beyond the essence.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود (Wajib al-Wujud)
قدم (qidam)
بقاء (baqa')
صفات سلبية (sifat salbiyya)
صفات ثبوتية (sifat thubutiyya)
أزلي (azali)
أبدي (abadi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qidam and baqa' are positive attributes that add something to Allah's essence beyond the essence itself.
Correction: The author shows they are negative attributes; they simply deny non-existence. Al-Turbashti's quote confirms they are names of the Essence, not separate positive attributes.

Checkpoint
Why does the author hold that pre-eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa') are negative attributes?
A) Because they affirm existence
B) Because they deny non-existence
C) Because they are not mentioned in the Qur'an
D) Because al-Turbashti said so

Key Takeaway
Qidam and baqa' in Allah are not positive attributes but simply negations of non-existence, making them negative attributes (sifat salbiyya).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm that Allah is Qadim (Pre-eternal) and Baqi (Permanent), do you realize that this means He has always existed and will always exist, while you came from nothing and will return to nothing without His sustaining power? How does this awareness of your absolute contingency shape your daily dependence on Him? Commit today to say 'Ya Qadim, Ya Baqi' with full consciousness that your existence is a gift sustained moment by moment.
?
If qidam and baqa' are merely negations of non-existence, then they tell you what Allah is not: He is not subject to beginning or end. How does this negative knowledge affect your worship? Are you tempted to imagine Allah in positive, human-like terms? Pledge to purify your concept of Allah by focusing on what He negates about Himself, and ask yourself: Do I truly worship a God beyond my imagination, or have I reduced Him to what I can comprehend?
?
Al-Turbashti said that 'the Existent' and 'the Pre-eternal' are names of the Essence itself, not separate attributes. This means that when you call upon Allah by these names, you are not appealing to a quality added to Him but to His very reality. How often do you invoke Allah's names as mere labels rather than as direct encounters with His essence? Beginning tomorrow, before each prayer, reflect on one of His names as a direct address to His very being, and note how it transforms your sense of connection.

The Negative Attributes of Pre-Eternity and Everlastingness
The commentator proves that pre-eternity and everlastingness are negative attributes negating non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why pre-eternity and everlastingness are considered negative attributes that negate non-existence, and how their meanings reduce to the negation of non-existence.

Core Idea
Qadim and baqi negate non-existence, not affirm a positive quality.

In this passage, the commentator argues that since Allah is the Necessary Existence, non-existence is impossible for Him, making Him pre-eternal and everlasting. These attributes do not add a positive quality but merely negate non-existence. Some scholars count them as positive, but the commentator shows that they reduce to negative attributes. We'll explore this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic once to get the flow, then read the translation. Notice the logical connector 'ثم لما ثبت'.
Pay attention to the terms 'قديم', 'باق', 'أزلي', 'أبدي'.
2
Understand the logical flow
Identify the premises: all things terminate to Necessary Existence, non-existence impossible, therefore He is azali/abadi, then qadim/baqi.
The argument moves from contingency to necessity to attributes.
3
Analyze the reduction to negative attributes
The commentator says qadim negates prior non-existence, baqi negates subsequent non-existence. Their meaning reduces to negation of non-existence. This makes them negative attributes.
Contrast with positive attributes like knowledge.
4
Reflect on the citation from al-Turpishti
Al-Turpishti says al-mawjud and al-qadim are names of the essence. Consider why he says this supports the negative interpretation.
This shows these are not additional qualifying attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما ثبت انتهاء الموجودات إلى واجب الوجود لذاته، والعدم على الواجب ممتنع، لأن ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه لزم كونه أزليا أبديا، فهو قديم لا أول لوجوده، وباق لا آخر لشهوده، فيرجع معنى القدم والبقاء في حقه سبحانه وتعالى إلى الصفات السلبية وإن عدهما بعضهم في النعوت الثبوتية؛ لأن معنى البقاء في حقه سبحانه وتعالى نفي عدم لاحق في الأبد، كما أن القدم عبارة عن نفي عدم سابق في الأزل فيرجع معناهما إلى نفي العدم، ولذا قال التوربشتي في معتقده: إن الموجود والقديم من أسماء الذات.
Then, when it is established that the existent things terminate to the Necessary Existence in essence, and non-existence upon the Necessary is impossible, because what is established in pre-eternity cannot cease to exist, it follows that He is eternal (azali) and everlasting (abadi). So He is pre-eternal (qadim) with no beginning to His existence, and everlasting (baqi) with no end to His everlastingness. Thus the meaning of pre-eternity and everlastingness in His right, glorified and exalted, reduces to the negative attributes, even though some count them among the positive attributes. Because the meaning of everlastingness in His right is the negation of subsequent non-existence in eternity, just as pre-eternity is an expression of the negation of prior non-existence in pre-eternity. So their meaning reduces to the negation of non-existence. Hence al-Turpishti said in his creed: 'The existent (al-mawjud) and the pre-eternal (al-qadim) are among the names of the essence.'
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a proof and definition. It begins by establishing that all contingent things terminate to a Necessary Existence (واجب الوجود). Non-existence is impossible for the Necessary, so it follows that He is eternal (azali) and everlasting (abadi). Therefore, He is qadim (no beginning) and baqi (no end). The commentator then argues that these attributes are negative (sifāt salbiyya) because they negate non-existence: qadim negates prior non-existence, baqi negates subsequent non-existence. Although some consider them positive attributes, their meaning reduces to the negation of non-existence. He then cites al-Turpishti who states that al-mawjud and al-qadim are names of the essence (dhāt), not additional attributes.

Key Terms

قديم
باق
أزلي
أبدي
صفات سلبية
نفي العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that 'qadim' and 'baqi' are positive attributes like knowledge or power, affirming a quality in Allah.
Correction: This passage shows that qadim and baqi simply negate non-existence (prior and subsequent), so they are negative attributes, not positive.

Checkpoint
What do the attributes 'qadim' and 'baqi' negate?
A) They affirm positive qualities.
B) They negate non-existence.
C) They negate creation.
D) They negate change.

Key Takeaway
Qadim and baqi are negative attributes that negate non-existence; they do not affirm a positive quality in Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's qadim and baqi merely negate non-existence, not add a quality, does that make you more or less in awe of His uniqueness? How does this shape your worship?
?

Refuting the Accusation of Anthropomorphism Against Ahl al-Sunna
The author refutes the Jahmiyya claim that Ahl al-Sunna are anthropomorphists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna refute the accusation of tashbih (anthropomorphism) by affirming attributes without resemblance, and how the Jahmiyya falsely label them as mushabbiha.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyya's accusation of tashbih is a false label; Ahl al-Sunna affirm attributes without resemblance.

The author addresses a persistent polemic: the Jahmiyya claim that Ahl al-Sunna are anthropomorphists because they affirm divine attributes. This passage clarifies that Ahl al-Sunna's position is actually the middle path — they affirm attributes while negating any resemblance to creation. The author supports this with Quranic evidence and quotes from early imams.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the full Arabic passage and its literal English translation to get an overall sense of the argument.
Notice the references to philosophers, Mu'tazila, Ash'aris, and early scholars.
2
Identify the groups and their positions
The passage summarizes how different groups handle divine attributes. Identify the philosophers, Mu'tazila, Ash'aris, and Ahl al-Sunna, and note their distinct approaches.
The Ash'aris are mentioned as negating both otherness and identity.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The author uses the verse 'There is nothing like Him' to negate likeness in essence or attributes. Understand the reasoning behind this proof and how it refutes tashbih.
The author also warns against misinterpreting the 'kaf' as superfluous.
4
Study the quotes from early imams
Nu'aym ibn Hammad and Ishaq ibn Rahawayh both affirm that likening Allah to creation is disbelief, but so is denying what Allah attributes to Himself. Understand how this establishes the middle path.
Their statements directly counter both extremes.
5
Recognize the polemical accusation
The passage identifies the sign of the Jahmiyya as falsely accusing Ahl al-Sunna of tashbih. This shows that the accusation is a rhetorical tool, not a genuine theological critique.
The passage ends by restating the Sunni position: negating tashbih does not mean negating attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل أن الفلاسفة والمعتزلة نفوا الصفات احترازاً عن تعدد القدماء وكذا الأشاعرة حيث ذهبوا إلى نفي غيريّتها وعينيتها في تحقيق الأسماء، ولا يشبهه شيء من خلقه) تأكيد لما قبله وتقرير لما قدمه وهو مستفاد من قوله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَىءٌ [الشورى: ۱۱]، أي كذاته أو صفاته، أو لأن نفي مثل المثل مستلزم لنفي المثل بطريق البرهان كما حققه بعض الأعيان ولا نقول بزيادة الكاف أو المثل لأن المثل المطلق هو المساوي من جميع الوجوه. قال نعيم بن حماد: من شبه الله بشيء من خلقه فقد كفر ومن أنكر ما وصف الله به نفسه فقد كفر. وقال إسحاق بن راهويه: من وصف الله فشبه صفاته بصفات من خلق الله فهو كافر بالله العظيم. وقال: علامة جهم وأصحابه دعواهم على أهل السنة والجماعة وما أولعوا به من الكذب أنهم مشبهة بل هم المعطلة، ولذا قال كثير من أئمة السلف: علامة الجهمية تسميتهم أهل السنة مشبهة، فإنه ما من أحد من نفاة الأسماء والصفات إلا يسمي من أثبتها مشبها حتى بعض المفسرين كعبد الجبار والزمخشري وغيرهما من المعتزلة والرافضة يسمون كل من أثبت شيئاً من الصفات أو قال برؤية الذات مشبهاً، والمشهور عند الجمهور من أهل السنة والجماعة أنهم لا يريدون بنفي التشبيه نفي الصفات، بل يريدون أنه سبحانه لا يشبه المخلوق في أسمائه وصفاته وأفعاله كما بينه الإمام بيانا شافيا.
The summary is that the philosophers and Mu'tazila negated the attributes to avoid multiplicity of eternal entities, and likewise the Ash'aris went to the negation of their otherness and identity in realizing the names. 'And nothing resembles Him from His creation' is an affirmation of what preceded and a confirmation of what he presented, and it is derived from His saying: 'There is nothing like Him' [al-Shura 11], meaning like His essence or His attributes, or because negation of the like of the like entails negation of the like by way of demonstration as verified by some eminent figures, and we do not say that the 'kaf' is extra or that 'like' is extra because the absolute 'like' is that which is equivalent in all respects. Nu'aym ibn Hammad said: 'Whoever likens Allah to anything of His creation has disbelieved, and whoever denies what Allah described Himself with has disbelieved.' Ishaq ibn Rahawayh said: 'Whoever describes Allah and likens His attributes to the attributes of His creation is a disbeliever in Allah Almighty.' And he said: 'The sign of Jahm and his followers is their claim against Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, and the lie they are fond of, that they are mushabbiha, but they are the mu'attila.' For this reason many of the salaf imams said: 'The sign of the Jahmiyya is that they call Ahl al-Sunna mushabbiha.' Indeed, there is no one among the deniers of names and attributes except that he calls the affirmers of them mushabbiha, even some exegetes like Abd al-Jabbar and al-Zamakhshari and others of the Mu'tazila and Rafida call everyone who affirms any attribute or says that the essence is seen a mushabbih. The well-known position among the general body of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that they do not intend by negating tashbih the negation of attributes, but rather they intend that He, glorified, does not resemble creation in His names, attributes, and actions, as the Imam clarified with a sufficient explanation.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the accusation of tashbih (anthropomorphism) leveled against Ahl al-Sunna. It begins with a summary: philosophers and Mu'tazila negated attributes to avoid multiplicity of eternal beings; the Ash'aris also negate both otherness and identity in the realization of names. Then it reaffirms 'nothing resembles Him from His creation' as a confirmation of the preceding, explaining that the verse 'There is nothing like Him' (al-Shura 11) negates likeness in essence or attributes, or that negating the like of the like entails negating the like by demonstration. It warns against interpreting the 'kaf' or 'like' as superfluous. Then it quotes Nu'aym ibn Hammad: both likening Allah to creation and denying what He attributes to Himself are disbelief. Ishaq ibn Rahawayh adds that describing Allah and likening His attributes to creation is disbelief. Then it notes that Jahm and his followers falsely accuse Ahl al-Sunna of being mushabbiha, while they themselves are the mu'attila (those who empty Allah of attributes). Many early imams stated that the sign of the Jahmiyya is that they call Ahl al-Sunna mushabbiha, for every denier of names and attributes calls the affirmers mushabbiha, even exegetes like Abd al-Jabbar and al-Zamakhshari and other Mu'tazila and Rafida. The well-known position of Ahl al-Sunna is that by negating tashbih they do not negate attributes, but rather affirm that Allah does not resemble creation in His names, attributes, and actions, as the Imam explained sufficiently.

Correction: Ahl al-Sunna affirm attributes while emphatically denying any resemblance to creation, and the accusation is a false label used by the Jahmiyya.

The Eternity of Allah's Attributes: Essential and Active
The author explains the eternity of essential and active attributes and the verbal nature of the dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between essential and active attributes, the Maturidi and Ash'ari positions, and why the dispute is considered verbal.

Core Idea
The dispute over active attributes is verbal; only their objects originate, not the attributes themselves.

This passage clarifies the nature of Allah's attributes, both essential and active, affirming their eternity and addressing a theological disagreement between the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools. The author argues that the dispute is merely verbal, and we will explore the rational and scriptural basis for this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage and its literal English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the flow from affirmation to explanation.
2
Distinguish essential and active attributes
Identify the two categories: essential (knowledge, life, speech) are eternal by consensus; active (creating, providing) are debated.
Essential attributes are inherent; active relate to manifestation.
3
Note the two schools' positions
The Maturidi school holds active attributes eternal, Ash'ari holds them originated. The author states the dispute is verbal according to precise investigators.
Verbal dispute means the difference is in terminology, not doctrine.
4
Study the explanation (bayān)
Work through the rational argument: Allah's essence suffices for all attributes, so no need for change. Also reflect on the Quranic verse supporting His self-sufficiency.
The key point: temporality of objects does not imply temporality of attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية والفعلية. (لم يزل) أي فيما مضى ولا يزال أي فيما يبقى (بأسمائه) أي منعوتا بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية كالعلم والحياة والكلام، وهي قديمة بالاتفاق والفعلية) أي موصوفا بصفاته الفعلية كالخلق والرزق ونحوهما، فمذهب الماتريدي أنها قديمة، ومذهب الأشاعرة أنها حادثة، والنزاع لفظي عند أرباب التدقيق كما يتبين عند التحقيق. وبيانه أن واجب الوجود لذاته واجب الوجود من جميع جهاته كأسمائه وصفاته والمعنى أنه ليست له صفة منتظرة ولا حالة متأخرة، إذ لیست ذاته محلا للأعراض فإن ذاته كافية في حصول جميع ما له من الصفات والحالات التي بها تتم الأعراض ولأنه لو لم تكن ذاته كافية في حصول ذلك لكانت محتاجة إلى ظهور الغير هنالك، وكل محتاج إلى الغير فهو ممكن الوجود، وقد ثبت أنه واجب الوجود، قال الله تعالى: يَاأَيُّهَا النَّاسُ أَنتُمُ الْفُقَرَاءُ إِلَى اللهِ وَاللهُ هُوَ الْغَنِيُّ الْحَمِيدُ [فاطر : ۱۵] أي غني لذاته وصفاته عن ظهور مصنوعاته، وهو حميد بنعوته وأسمائه سواء حمده أو لم يحمده أحد من سواه، فهو منزه عن التغير والانتقال بل لا يزال في نعوته الفعلية منزها عن الزوال وفي صفاته الذاتية مستغنيا عن الاستكمال، ولا يلزم من حدوث متعلقات هذه الصفات حدوث الصفات كالمخلوق والمرزوق والمسموع والمبصر وسائر الكائنات وجميع المعلومات.
He has never ceased and will not cease [to be described] with His names and His essential and active attributes. 'Has never ceased' meaning in the past, and 'will not cease' meaning in the future, 'with His names' meaning described by His names and essential attributes like knowledge, life, and speech, and they are eternal by agreement, and 'active' meaning described by His active attributes like creating, providing, and the like. The Maturidi school holds that they are eternal, and the Ash'ari school holds that they are originated, and the dispute is verbal according to the precise investigators as becomes clear upon investigation. Its explanation is that the Necessary of Existence by His essence is Necessary of Existence from all His aspects, like His names and attributes. The meaning is that He has no pending attribute nor later state, since His essence is not a locus for accidents, for His essence suffices for the occurrence of all the attributes and states through which the accidents are completed. And because if His essence were not sufficient for that occurrence, it would be in need of the manifestation of something else, and everything in need of something else is possible of existence, and it has been established that He is Necessary of Existence. Allah said: 'O mankind, you are the poor in need of Allah, and Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Praiseworthy' [Fatir 15], meaning self-sufficient in His essence and attributes from the manifestation of His creations, and He is praiseworthy by His characteristics and names whether anyone praises Him or not. He is free from change and transition; rather, He never ceases to be in His active characteristics free from cessation, and in His essential attributes self-sufficient from completion. The origination of the objects of these attributes does not entail the origination of the attributes, like the created, the provided, the heard, the seen, and all other beings and all known things.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage discusses the eternity of Allah's attributes. It begins by affirming that Allah has always been and will always be with His names and attributes, both essential (like knowledge, life, speech) and active (like creating, providing). The essential attributes are agreed to be eternal. For the active attributes, the Maturidi school holds they are eternal, while the Ash'ari school holds they are originated (haditha). However, the author states that this dispute is verbal (lafzi) according to the precise investigators, meaning it is not a real theological difference but one of terminology. Then follows the explanation (bayān): The Necessary Being is necessary in all aspects, including His names and attributes. He has no pending attribute or later state because His essence is not a locus for accidents. His essence is sufficient for all His attributes and states; if it were not sufficient, it would need something else, which would make it contingent, contradicting His necessity. The Quranic verse 'O mankind, you are the poor in need of Allah, and Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Praiseworthy' (Fatir 15) is cited to show His self-sufficiency. Allah is free from change and transition; He is always in His active attributes without cessation and in His essential attributes without need for completion. The key point is that the origination of the objects of these attributes (e.g., created things, provided things, things heard, things seen) does not entail the origination of the attributes themselves. For example, the fact that creatures are created does not mean that the attribute of 'creating' is originated; rather, the attribute is eternal while its objects are temporal.

Key Terms
الصفات الذاتية
الصفات الفعلية
الماتريدي
الأشاعرة
النزاع لفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because the objects of active attributes (e.g., created things) originate in time, the attributes themselves must also be originated, implying change in Allah.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only the objects change; the attributes remain eternal. Allah's essence is sufficient for all attributes, so no change occurs.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of the Maturidis regarding the active attributes (al-sifat al-fi'liyya)?
A) They are eternal (qadima)
B) They are originated (haditha)
C) They are neither eternal nor originated
D) The dispute is verbal

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are eternal; only their temporal objects change, so the dispute between Maturidis and Ash'aris is verbal, not substantive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is self-sufficient and does not need His creation, yet you constantly seek His help, does your need for Him ever reach a point where you feel you are imposing on Him? How does knowing that your need does not change His attributes affect your dua?
?
The passage says Allah's attributes are eternal and unchanging even as His creatures constantly change. In what areas of your life do you act as if you can change Allah's will or attributes by your own efforts? What would it mean to truly trust that His attributes are fixed and perfect?
?
The dispute about active attributes is said to be verbal, not substantive. Are there beliefs you hold about Allah that are actually just a matter of wording, yet you treat them as fundamental differences? Could you surrender those verbal distinctions for the sake of unity?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
The Eternity of God's Names and Self-Attributes
Commentary explains the eternity of attributes and the dispute over active attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of God's eternal names and attributes, the distinction between self-attributes and active attributes, and the different scholarly positions on active attributes.

Core Idea
God's names and self-attributes are eternal; the dispute over active attributes is verbal.

This lesson unpacks the opening statement of the passage, which affirms that God has always been and will always be with His names and attributes. It clarifies the two categories of attributes—self-attributes (dhatiyya) and active attributes (fi'liyya)—and introduces the Maturidi-Ash'ari debate over whether active attributes are eternal or originated.

Guided Path
1
Understand the statement 'Lam yazal wa la yazal'
Read the first sentence carefully and note that it affirms God's eternal existence with His names and attributes.
The phrase covers both past and future eternity.
2
Distinguish between self-attributes and active attributes
Identify the two categories mentioned: self-attributes (like knowledge, life, speech) and active attributes (like creating, providing).
Self-attributes are eternal by consensus.
3
Learn the Maturidi and Ash'ari positions
Note that the Maturidis consider active attributes eternal, while the Ash'aris consider them originated. The passage calls this dispute 'verbal' among verifiers.
This sets the stage for the later proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية والفعلية. المعتزلة والرافضة يسمون كل من أثبت شيئاً من الصفات أو قال برؤية الذات مشبهاً، والمشهور عند الجمهور من أهل السنة والجماعة أنهم لا يريدون بنفي التشبيه نفي الصفات، بل يريدون أنه سبحانه لا يشبه المخلوق في أسمائه وصفاته وأفعاله كما بينه الإمام بيانا شافيا. (لم يزل) أي فيما مضى ولا يزال أي فيما يبقى (بأسمائه) أي منعوتا بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية كالعلم والحياة والكلام، وهي قديمة بالاتفاق والفعلية) أي موصوفا بصفاته الفعلية كالخلق والرزق ونحوهما، فمذهب الماتريدي أنها قديمة، ومذهب الأشاعرة أنها حادثة، والنزاع لفظي عند أرباب التدقيق كما يتبين عند التحقيق. وبيانه أن واجب الوجود لذاته واجب الوجود من جميع جهاته كأسمائه وصفاته والمعنى أنه ليست له صفة منتظرة ولا حالة متأخرة، إذ لیست ذاته محلا للأعراض فإن ذاته كافية في حصول جميع ما له من الصفات والحالات التي بها تتم الأعراض ولأنه لو لم تكن ذاته كافية في حصول ذلك لكانت محتاجة إلى ظهور الغير هنالك، وكل محتاج إلى الغير فهو ممكن الوجود، وقد ثبت أنه واجب الوجود، قال الله تعالى: يَاأَيُّهَا النَّاسُ أَنتُمُ الْفُقَرَاءُ إِلَى اللهِ وَاللهُ هُوَ الْغَنِيُّ الْحَمِيدُ [فاطر : ١٥] أي غني لذاته وصفاته عن ظهور مصنوعاته، وهو حميد بنعوته وأسمائه سواء حمده أو لم يحمده أحد من سواه، فهو منزه عن التغير والانتقال بل لا يزال في نعوته الفعلية منزها عن الزوال وفي صفاته الذاتية مستغنيا عن الاستكمال، ولا يلزم من حدوث متعلقات هذه الصفات حدوث الصفات كالمخلوق والمرزوق والمسموع والمبصر وسائر الكائنات وجميع المعلومات.
He [God] has not ceased nor will He cease with His names and His self-attributes and active attributes. The Mu'tazila and the Rafida call everyone who affirms any of the attributes or says that the essence is seen a 'musabbih' (anthropomorphist). The well-known position of the majority of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that by negating tashbih they do not intend negation of the attributes; rather they intend that He, exalted, does not resemble the creation in His names, attributes, and actions, as the Imam explained clearly. ('Lam yazal' means in the past, 'wa la yazal' means in the future. 'Bi-asma'ihi' means described by His names and self-attributes such as knowledge, life, and speech, which are eternal by consensus. 'Wa al-fi'liyya' means described by His active attributes such as creating, providing, and the like. The Maturidi school holds that they are eternal, while the Ash'ari school holds that they are originated. The dispute is verbal among the masters of verification, as will become clear upon investigation. Its explanation: The Necessary Existence by virtue of Its essence is Necessary Existence from all Its aspects, such as Its names and attributes. The meaning is that He has no pending attribute nor subsequent state, since His essence is not a locus for accidents. For His essence is sufficient for the attainment of all His attributes and states through which accidents are perfected. Because if His essence were not sufficient for attaining that, it would be in need of the appearance of something else, and everything in need of something else is possible of existence, and it has been established that He is the Necessary Existence. Allah, exalted, says: 'O people, you are the poor to Allah, and Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Praiseworthy' (Quran 35:15). Meaning He is self-sufficient in His essence and attributes from the appearance of His creations, and He is praiseworthy in His qualities and names, whether anyone praises Him or not. He is transcendent above change and transition; rather He continues in His active qualities, transcendent above disappearance, and in His self-attributes, independent of perfection. The temporality of the objects of these attributes does not necessitate the temporality of the attributes, such as the created, the provided, the heard, the seen, and all other existents and all known things.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement 'لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية والفعلية.' It begins by addressing the Mu'tazila and Rafida who accuse anyone who affirms attributes or believes in the vision of God of anthropomorphism (tashbih). The author clarifies that Ahl al-Sunna, in negating tashbih, do not negate the attributes; rather they affirm that God does not resemble creation in any of His names, attributes, or actions. The author then explains the phrase 'لم يزل ولا يزال' as referring to the past and future eternity of God's names and attributes. He distinguishes between self-attributes (such as knowledge, life, speech) which are eternal by consensus, and active attributes (such as creating, providing) concerning which there is a difference: the Maturidis hold them eternal, the Ash'aris hold them originated. However, the author notes that this dispute is merely verbal among the verifiers. He then provides a proof that God, being the Necessary Existent, does not have pending or subsequent qualities, for His essence is sufficient and not a locus for accidents. If His essence were in need of something else, it would be contingent. He quotes the verse from Surah Fatir (35:15) to show God's self-sufficiency. He concludes that temporality of the objects of attributes does not entail temporality of the attributes themselves.

Key Terms
الصفات الذاتية
الصفات الفعلية
الماتريدي
الأشاعرة
النزاع اللفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which school holds that active attributes are eternal?
A) Ash'ari
B) Maturidi
C) Mu'tazila
D) Rafida

Key Takeaway
God's self-attributes are eternal by consensus, while the debate over active attributes is ultimately verbal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You affirm that God's attributes are eternal. But when you face hardship, do you truly trust that His mercy and power are as constant today as they ever were? What would change in your life if you fully internalized that His self-attributes never waver?
?
The scholars' dispute over active attributes is called 'verbal'—meaning they agree in substance. Are there disagreements you have with others where the real issue is just wording? Can you let go of the need to be right and seek the common ground?
?
Knowing that God is described by both eternal self-attributes and temporal active attributes, which of His eternal attributes do you most need to lean on right now? How can you actively remember that attribute throughout your day?

Divine Attributes
beginner

The Refutation of Tashbih: Affirming Attributes without Anthropomorphism
Commentary refutes the accusation of anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position on tashbih: they negate any resemblance between God and creation while affirming His attributes.

Core Idea
Negating tashbih does not mean negating God's attributes.

This lesson addresses a common accusation by the Mu'tazila and Rafida against those who affirm God's attributes or believe in seeing Him. The commentator explains that Ahl al-Sunna's negation of tashbih is not a denial of attributes but a denial of any similarity between the Creator and creation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the accusation by the Mu'tazila and Rafida
They call anyone who affirms attributes or believes in the vision of God a 'musabbih' (anthropomorphist).
This accusation misrepresents the Sunni position.
2
Understand the Ahl al-Sunna response
Ahl al-Sunna clarify that they negate tashbih as resemblance, not as negation of attributes. They affirm that God does not resemble creation in any way.
The commentator notes the Imam gave a clear explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية والفعلية. المعتزلة والرافضة يسمون كل من أثبت شيئاً من الصفات أو قال برؤية الذات مشبهاً، والمشهور عند الجمهور من أهل السنة والجماعة أنهم لا يريدون بنفي التشبيه نفي الصفات، بل يريدون أنه سبحانه لا يشبه المخلوق في أسمائه وصفاته وأفعاله كما بينه الإمام بيانا شافيا. (لم يزل) أي فيما مضى ولا يزال أي فيما يبقى (بأسمائه) أي منعوتا بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية كالعلم والحياة والكلام، وهي قديمة بالاتفاق والفعلية) أي موصوفا بصفاته الفعلية كالخلق والرزق ونحوهما، فمذهب الماتريدي أنها قديمة، ومذهب الأشاعرة أنها حادثة، والنزاع لفظي عند أرباب التدقيق كما يتبين عند التحقيق. وبيانه أن واجب الوجود لذاته واجب الوجود من جميع جهاته كأسمائه وصفاته والمعنى أنه ليست له صفة منتظرة ولا حالة متأخرة، إذ لیست ذاته محلا للأعراض فإن ذاته كافية في حصول جميع ما له من الصفات والحالات التي بها تتم الأعراض ولأنه لو لم تكن ذاته كافية في حصول ذلك لكانت محتاجة إلى ظهور الغير هنالك، وكل محتاج إلى الغير فهو ممكن الوجود، وقد ثبت أنه واجب الوجود، قال الله تعالى: يَاأَيُّهَا النَّاسُ أَنتُمُ الْفُقَرَاءُ إِلَى اللهِ وَاللهُ هُوَ الْغَنِيُّ الْحَمِيدُ [فاطر : ١٥] أي غني لذاته وصفاته عن ظهور مصنوعاته، وهو حميد بنعوته وأسمائه سواء حمده أو لم يحمده أحد من سواه، فهو منزه عن التغير والانتقال بل لا يزال في نعوته الفعلية منزها عن الزوال وفي صفاته الذاتية مستغنيا عن الاستكمال، ولا يلزم من حدوث متعلقات هذه الصفات حدوث الصفات كالمخلوق والمرزوق والمسموع والمبصر وسائر الكائنات وجميع المعلومات.

The meaning is that He has no pending attribute nor subsequent state, since His essence is not a locus for accidents. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that negating tashbih means denying God's attributes.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna affirm attributes while denying any resemblance to creation.

Checkpoint
What do the Mu'tazila and Rafida call those who affirm attributes?
A) Mushabbihun
B) Mu'attila
C) Jahmiyya
D) Qadariyya

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna negate tashbih as resemblance, not as denial of attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Mu'tazila and Rafida label others as musabbih. When you discuss theological issues, are you quick to label someone as extreme or deviant without first understanding their actual position? How can you change this habit?
?
The lesson teaches that negating tashbih does not mean negating attributes. Is there a concept in your own life where you have overcorrected—perhaps avoiding one extreme by falling into another? How can you seek balance in your understanding of God?
?
The Ahl al-Sunna affirm that God does not resemble creation in names, attributes, and actions. Do you truly internalise this, or do you sometimes imagine God in anthropomorphic ways despite knowing better? What concrete step can you take to purify your conception of God?

Divine Attributes

The Proof: God's Essence is Sufficient and His Attributes are Eternal
Commentary provides a rational proof for the sufficiency of God's essence and the eternity of attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that God's essence is sufficient for all His attributes, and that the temporality of created things does not affect the eternity of His attributes.

Core Idea
God's essence needs nothing; the creation of accidents does not imply change in Him.

This lesson presents the logical proof that the Necessary Existent must be sufficient in its essence for all its attributes. It explains that if God were not sufficient, He would be in need of something else, which contradicts His necessity. The passage also asserts that the temporal origination of the objects of God's actions (like created beings) does not make His own attributes temporal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle: the Necessary Existent is necessary from all aspects
God's necessity extends to His names and attributes; He has no pending attribute or subsequent state.
This means His essence is not a locus for accidents.
2
Follow the argument from contingency
If God's essence were not sufficient for His attributes, it would need something else, making it contingent—contradicting His necessity.
The Quranic verse (35:15) supports His self-sufficiency.
3
Learn the conclusion: temporality of effects does not affect attributes
The creation of things like the created, provided, heard, etc. does not make God's attributes temporal.
God remains transcendent above change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته الذاتية والفعلية. المعتزلة والرافضة يسمون كل من أثبت شيئاً من الصفات أو قال برؤية الذات مشبهاً، والمشهور عند الجمهور من أهل السنة والجماعة أنهم لا يريدون بنفي التشبيه نفي الصفات، بل يريدون أنه سبحانه لا يشبه المخلوق في أسمائه وصفاته وأفعاله كما بينه الإمام بيانا شافيا. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates temporal things, then His attributes (like creating) must be temporal.
Correction: The temporality of the objects of attributes does not entail the temporality of the attributes themselves.

Checkpoint
What would follow if God's essence were not sufficient for His attributes?
A) He would be possible of existence
B) He would be eternal
C) He would be transcendent
D) He would be self-sufficient

Key Takeaway
God's essence is self-sufficient; the creation of temporal things does not affect the eternity of His attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live your daily life as someone who is 'poor to Allah' (al-fuqara' ila Allah) or do you often feel self-sufficient in your own ability? How does recognizing God's absolute self-sufficiency change the way you approach your needs and desires today?
?
The passage states that God is praiseworthy whether anyone praises Him or not. How does this reality confront your motivation for worship? Do you worship Him for His sake or for your own benefit?
?
If God's attributes are eternal and unaffected by the temporality of their objects, how should this shape your trust in His attributes of hearing, seeing, and providing? Are you acting as if God's seeing and hearing are dependent on what you do, or are you living secure in His eternal awareness?

The Three Self-Attributes: Life, Power, and Knowledge
Commentary defines the three self-attributes: life, power, and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three self-attributes of Allah—life, power, and knowledge—as eternal attributes that define His essence.

Core Idea
Allah's self-attributes—life, power, knowledge—are eternal and define His essence.

The commentary now turns to the self-attributes (sifāt dhātiyya), which are those attributes that are inseparable from Allah's essence. In this passage, the author explains the three consensual self-attributes: life, power, and knowledge. Each is defined as an eternal attribute with distinct implications for Allah's actions and knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own definitions come through before you interpret.
Notice that each attribute is introduced with 'هي صفة أزلية' (it is an eternal attribute).
2
Identify and understand each attribute
The passage presents three self-attributes: life, power, and knowledge. For each, note how it is defined and what it entails. Life necessitates soundness of knowledge; power affects objects of power; knowledge discloses information.
The definitions are concise but profound.
3
Reflect on the eternal nature
All three attributes are described as 'azaliyya' (eternal). Consider why this is important: it means they are not acquired or temporal, but essential to Allah.
This guards against the misconception that attributes are accidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفات الذاتية والفعلية. أما الذاتية فالحياة والقدرة والعلم (أما الذاتية) أي الإجماعية (فالحياة وهي صفة أزلية تقتضي صحة العلم لموصوفها (والقدرة) أي وكذا القدرة صفة أزلية تؤثر في المقدورات عند تعلقها بها، والمعنى أن الله تعالى حي بحياته التي هي صفته الأزلية الأبدية وقادر بقدرته التي هي صفته الأزلية السرمدية، للأشياء الممكنة، فهو الحي القيوم، أي القائم بذاته المقيم لموجوداته، وأنه يحيي الموتى من العدم بداية ومن بعد إماتتهم إعادة وهو على كل شيء قدير، حيث خلق الخلق وأعطاهم الحياة والقدرة والرزق ومعنى كونه قادرا أن يصح منه إيجاد العالم وتركه. (والعلم) أي من الصفات الذاتية وهي صفة أزلية تنكشف المعلومات عند تعلقها بها، فالله تعالى عالم بجميع الموجودات لا يعزب عن علمه مثقال ذرة في العلويات والسفليات، وأنه تعالى يعلم الجهر والسر وما يكون أخفى منه من المغيبات، بل أحاط بكل شيء علما من الجزئيات والكليات والموجودات والمعدومات والممكنات والمستحيلات فهو بكل شيء عليم من الذوات والصفات بعلم قديم لم يزل موصوفا به على وجه الكمال لا يعلم حادث حاصل في ذاته بالقبول والانفعال والتغير والانتقال، تعالى الله ذلك شأنه وتعظم عما نهاك برهانه.
Self-attributes and active attributes. As for the self-attributes, they are life, power, and knowledge. (As for the self-attributes) i.e., the consensual ones, (life) is an eternal attribute that necessitates the soundness of knowledge for its possessor. (And power) i.e., similarly, power is an eternal attribute that affects the objects of power when it is attached to them. The meaning is that Allah, exalted, is alive with His life which is His eternal attribute, and is powerful with His power which is His eternal attribute, for possible things. He is the Living, the Self-Subsisting, i.e., the self-subsisting, the one who sustains His existents. And He gives life to the dead from non-existence initially, and after their death, He returns them, and He has power over all things, as He created creation and gave them life, power, and provision. The meaning of His being powerful is that the origination of the world and its abandonment are possible from Him. (And knowledge) is one of the self-attributes, an eternal attribute by which information is disclosed when it is attached to them. Allah, exalted, is knower of all existents; not even an atom's weight escapes His knowledge in the heavens and the earth. And He knows the open and the secret and what is more hidden than that from the unseen. Rather, He encompasses all things in knowledge, from particulars and universals, existents and non-existents, possibles and impossibles. So He is Knower of all things, of essences and attributes, with an eternal knowledge with which He has never ceased to be described in a perfect manner; no temporal event occurs in His essence by way of reception, passivity, change, or transition. Exalted is Allah, that is His majesty, and great is His proof against you.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the three self-attributes: life, power, and knowledge. It first states that the self-attributes are life, power, and knowledge, and they are consensual among Muslims. Life is defined as an eternal attribute that makes knowledge valid for its possessor. Power is an eternal attribute that affects objects of power when attached to them. God is alive and powerful by these eternal attributes. The author then elaborates on God's power: He is the Living, Self-Subsisting, who gives life and causes death, and has power over all things. Knowledge is an eternal attribute that reveals information. God knows all things—particulars and universals, existents and non-existents, possibles and impossibles—with an eternal perfect knowledge, without any change or passivity in His essence. The passage concludes by exalting God above any imperfection.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might assume that divine attributes are accidental or temporal.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that all three self-attributes are eternal (azaliyya), not acquired or subject to change.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the attribute of life necessitate?
A) The soundness of power
B) The soundness of knowledge
C) The creation of the world
D) The ability to see

Key Takeaway
The three self-attributes of life, power, and knowledge are eternal and essential to Allah's nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's power is eternal and affects every possible thing, what specific burden from today would you entrust to Him right now?
?
Since Allah's knowledge encompasses every thought you have ever had or will have, how does that change the way you speak, act, or even think in private?
?
Knowing that Allah's life is eternal and that He never changes, does your relationship with Him reflect that stability, or do you treat Him as if He is distant and indifferent?

The Positive Nature of Knowledge: Imam Abdul Aziz's Debate
Anecdote of a debate on the attribute of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of knowledge is a positive attribute of perfection, not merely the absence of ignorance.

Core Idea
Knowledge is a positive attribute, not just negation of ignorance.

Imam Abdul Aziz al-Makki, a companion of Imam al-Shafi'i, debated Bishr al-Marisi before Caliph al-Ma'mun. Bishr claimed that God is 'not ignorant,' but Imam Abdul Aziz countered that negating ignorance is not praiseworthy because even an inanimate object lacks ignorance. This anecdote illustrates a key theological principle: God's attributes are positive and real.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the flow: Bishr's statement, then Imam Abdul Aziz's response.
The passage is an anecdote; pay attention to the argument.
2
Understand Bishr's position
Bishr al-Marisi says 'I say that He is not ignorant.' This is a negation-based description of God.
This reflects a Mu'tazili approach of describing God by negating imperfections.
3
Analyze Imam Abdul Aziz's counterargument
He rejects that negation alone is praiseworthy, using the example of a column which is also not ignorant. Then he points out that Allah praised prophets, angels, and believers by affirming knowledge, not by negating ignorance.
This shows that knowledge is an affirmed positive attribute.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
The debate teaches that divine attributes are positive and real qualities, not mere negations. This is a fundamental principle in Sunni theology.
Consider why this matters for understanding God's perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام عبد العزيز المكي صاحب الإمام الشافعي وجليسه في كتابه الذي حكي فيه علمه تعالى فقال بشر: أقول لا يجهل، مناظرته لبشر المريسي عند المأمون حين سأله عن فجعل يكرر السؤال عن صفة العلم تقريراً له، فقال الإمام عبد العزيز: نفي الجهل لا يكون صفة مدح فإن هذه الأسطوانة لا تجهل، وقد مدح الله تعالى الأنبياء والملائكة والمؤمنين بالعلم
Imam Abdul Aziz al-Makki, the companion and close associate of Imam al-Shafi'i, said in his book in which he reported his knowledge of Allah, exalted: Bishr said: 'I say that He is not ignorant.' His debate with Bishr al-Marisi before al-Ma'mun when he (al-Ma'mun) asked about... and he kept repeating the question about the attribute of knowledge to ascertain it. Imam Abdul Aziz said: 'Negation of ignorance is not a praiseworthy attribute, for this column is not ignorant. And Allah, exalted, has praised the prophets, angels, and believers with knowledge.'
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage narrates a debate between Imam Abdul Aziz al-Makki and Bishr al-Marisi (a Mu'tazili) before Caliph al-Ma'mun. Bishr said 'I say that He (God) is not ignorant.' Imam Abdul Aziz responded that merely negating ignorance is not a praiseworthy attribute because even an inanimate object like a column is not ignorant. Rather, God has praised the prophets, angels, and believers by affirming knowledge for them, implying that knowledge is a positive attribute of perfection, not merely the absence of ignorance. This anecdote illustrates that the attribute of knowledge is a distinct positive attribute, not reducible to negation of its opposite.

Key Terms
العلم
نفي الجهل
الإمام عبد العزيز المكي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God's knowledge is merely the absence of ignorance.
Correction: The anecdote shows that negation of ignorance is not praiseworthy; knowledge is a positive attribute affirmed by scripture for prophets, angels, and believers.

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Abdul Aziz reject Bishr's statement that God is not ignorant?
A) Because ignorance is impossible for God
B) Because negation of ignorance is not a praiseworthy attribute
C) Because God is ignorant
D) Because Bishr was lying

Key Takeaway
Divine attributes like knowledge are positive and real, not mere negations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often hear 'Allah knows everything.' But do you truly believe that His knowledge is a real, positive attribute, or do you merely think of it as 'He's not ignorant'? How does this affect the way you trust His knowledge in your daily decisions?
?
If you only think of God in terms of what He is not (not ignorant, not weak, etc.), are you missing out on praising Him with positive attributes? What is one positive attribute of Allah that you can focus on today in your prayer?
?
Imam Abdul Aziz used a column as an example to show that mere negation is not praise. What in your life is like that column—something that lacks ignorance but does not deserve praise? How can you move from mere negation to genuine affirmation in your relationship with Allah?
